    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124557147?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Akaria Gale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Akaria Gale" href="/user/show/3895495-akaria-gale">Akaria Gale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3895495-akaria-gale?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124557147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15648273235082026795">It's official. I love the Breed! After finding the previous two books a little lacking it was so satisfying to see Adrian finally hit it out of the park with Tegan and Elise. The couple is matched perfectly. Both of them have lost mates due to the war with the Rogues. Most recently, Elise also lost her son to the drug Crimson. They know pain loss and Tegan especially understands Elise's need to kill as many Minions as she can. He's been filled with the same need for the past five hundred years.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText15648273235082026795" style="display:none">It's official. I love the Breed! After finding the previous two books a little lacking it was so satisfying to see Adrian finally hit it out of the park with Tegan and Elise. The couple is matched perfectly. Both of them have lost mates due to the war with the Rogues. Most recently, Elise also lost her son to the drug Crimson. They know pain loss and Tegan especially understands Elise's need to kill as many Minions as she can. He's been filled with the same need for the past five hundred years.<br /><br />The romance builds quickly but more believably than in past books. Elise has already been a part of the Breed world for around a hundred years so we could skip the whole "OMG vampires exist?" drama. Elise is strong and capable but unlike the past two heroines she has no TSTL moment of leaving the Order's super secure compound only to get herself kidnapped. While I liked Tegan a great deal he seemed a little too much like the cookie cutter hardened badass. Even though this series focuses more on the men, I found Elise's journey to accept love again much more interesting than Tegan's. <br /><br />My favorite scene in the series so far happens towards the end and sealed the deal with me and the Breed. Breedmates all have special gifts and watching the women work together using their gifts to solve an important piece of the puzzle won me over right there. In so many other series involving warriors the females disappear or don't really have a role to play in the battle against evil. Not so in the Order. Through their special talents the Breedmates can contribute to the cause without being on the front line.<br /><br />Adrian keeps giving me more and more of what I love about this series. A diverse cast of warriors, empowered females and a new great evil that makes Marek look like a declawed kitten. She's also introduced yet another character I can't wait to get more of. German playboy Andreas. I'm such a sucker for stories of a gigolo who meets that one woman he can't live without.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15648273235082026795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13309464274673287167" style="display:none"><b>3 star rating!</b><br /><br />Maybe I did a mistake jumping right on book number 3 in the series but the blurb was great, so I decided to start from there.<br /><br />The plot was very interesting. I like to read paranormal books once in a while and the start was promising. But in the half of the book I felt kind of tired. The author's describing the main characters was different from what their actions spoke to me. I was feeling something else, my impression was different. For example the main character Elise was described as a strong willed heroine, which I did understand since the big amount of loss she has suffered in her life. But her interactions with Tegan spoke to me that she was not. And I have to say I didn't like her at all.<br /><br />I had some mixed feelings about Tegan as well. I didn't loved him, but I didn't hate him as well. The chemistry between them wasn't intense or maybe I didn't catch it all.<br /><br />The plot was very interesting and the writing was very good. Probably the characters in the book just didn't gave me what I wanted at that time.<br /> </span>

<div id="review_1109787677" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109787677" />
    <a title="Naomi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20128361-naomi"><img alt="Naomi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418567627p2/20128361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109787677?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi" href="/user/show/20128361-naomi">Naomi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=tattooed-and-pierced">tattooed-and-pierced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=alpha-males">alpha-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=big-bad-vampires">big-bad-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=lara-adrian">lara-adrian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109787677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11239136265274084651">Midnight Awakening was incredible! This book was different than the first two, in a good way. Even though I loved Kiss of Midnight and Kiss of Crimson, Midnight Awakening is a very powerful story with two amazing main characters.<br/><br/>The MCs are super important for me (and for everyone I guess), but most of the time, I don’t love the MCs the same. I always prefer the hero. But in this book, I really loved them both. Tegan and Elise are awesome and their story was so good! I’ve said it before and I’ll</span>
  <span id="freeText11239136265274084651" style="display:none">Midnight Awakening was incredible! This book was different than the first two, in a good way. Even though I loved Kiss of Midnight and Kiss of Crimson, Midnight Awakening is a very powerful story with two amazing main characters.<br /><br />The MCs are super important for me (and for everyone I guess), but most of the time, I don’t love the MCs the same. I always prefer the hero. But in this book, I really loved them both. Tegan and Elise are awesome and their story was so good! I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again, Lara’s writing style is magic! She made Tegan’s story very special and she gets better with every book she writes.<br /><br />Tegan is a very dark and cold character and Elise is the complete opposite. She’s innocent and compassionate. But, like I said, Lara did such a great job with them. They truly are perfect for each other, they complete each other and I loved reading their story! Elise was such a surprise, she’s so much more than what I thought. After the death of her son (in Kiss of Crimson), Elise is decided to avenge him and her late husband. She is such a brave woman, I was in awe of her. I loved her determination, she was smart and she did not do anything stupid and YAY for that! But Elise is also a fragile female, her special ability to hear the thoughts of humans is really hard on her and five long years without vampire blood is making her weak.<br />Tegan is so different from her, he’s ice, he doesn’t feel anything, he lives to kill Rogues and he’s a loner. I was also super surprised with him, I knew I was going to like him but I did much more than that, I freaking love him! Tegan is a very complex character, he has a very heavy past and he’s just so wounded. He wants to protect himself by distancing himself from everyone.<br /><br />They formed the perfect couple. Lara brought them together slowly, smartly. She did it so well! It was not easy but it was worth it. I loved Elise even more for her tenacity, sure she had her doubts at some point, which is understandable but she never gave up on Tegan, she stayed by his side and her love for him was beautiful. Tegan was more difficult, after all these years of loneliness, it was not easy for him to open up to someone else. At times, I admit it, I wanted to shake some sense into him, he could be such an asshole with her but then he would do something super sweet and so unexpected of him, I couldn’t stay mad!<br /><br />When they truly were together, it was perfect! I actually had time to enjoy them as a couple, for once, Lara brought the two main characters together before the ending and that’s a great thing! The sex scenes were also steamier and oh my, yes!<br /><br />The plot in Midnight Awakening was better as well! It was very interesting and more complex. And the ending killed me! I really want to read Rio’s book now. I liked the plot because it was a good part of the story and even though the romance was the main focus, the plot was important. It was intriguing and I was so freaking excited when Elise found out about the tapestry! You should have seen me, I was ridiculous, all alone is my bed, squealing like a crazy person… that’s what books will do to you at 4 am in the morning! Anyway, Lara sure did a better job, for me, with the plot in this book. The ending was perfect, the suspense is killing me!<br /><br />However, I was a little bit disappointed because I was expecting more from Tegan and Lucan’s reconciliation. In the first two books, Tegan hates Lucan and Lucan is pissed at Tegan for doing everything solo. And they have a past, I mean, I was expecting more. Sure, they had a little talk but that’s all and I admit, I was disappointed. I wanted more anger, more yelling, more everything. But hey! I guess, I can’t have everything! I was also expecting more of Tegan, I mean, same here, in the first two books he’s depicted as such a fierce, hard, unfeeling, mean warrior, and, sure he is, in some ways, but I would have liked more of all of this. In this book, he seemed more human, less cold and I was surprised by this. But, once again, a book can’t be perfect. And those are details who didn’t truly impact in the story (and it’s also a personal point of view).<br /><br />We also meet some new secondary characters in this book, who will have their own book in the future and I can’t wait! I came to actually care a little about Sterling Chase. I just pity the guy. He’s clearly miserable and I think he deserves to find some happiness and love. Next is Rio’s book and I am so freaking excited because I absolutely love Rio and he so deserves some love and happiness too! <br /><br />This series is a very good one and, I know lots of people don’t read it because of the BDB series and the comparisons, I was one of those people before, the BDB series will always by my favorite series in the whole world, but, trust me, the Midnight Breed series is its own series and it’s really worth the read as well! I promise you will not regret it. Lara is a great and unique writer, give her a chance!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11239136265274084651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103518956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103518956" />
    <a title="Soraia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3717008-soraia"><img alt="Soraia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298432311p2/3717008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103518956?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soraia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soraia" href="/user/show/3717008-soraia">Soraia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3717008-soraia?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3717008-soraia?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3717008-soraia?shelf=paranormal-series">paranormal-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3717008-soraia?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3717008-soraia?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103518956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13780712484784841904">The Midnight Breed series is something that requires patience. <br/><br/>On the first book you get a rough story, with not much of a plot line and lots of unexplained details. The heroine, Gabrielle, is nothing interesting, the conflicts are not well justified and the hero's nine hundred years of past are just boring. <br/><br/>The second book gets a little better. The heroine is more charming with a better constructed past, an amazing breedmate ability but still a little annoying. Dante, the hero, is less conflict</span>
  <span id="freeText13780712484784841904" style="display:none">The Midnight Breed series is something that requires patience. <br /><br />On the first book you get a rough story, with not much of a plot line and lots of unexplained details. The heroine, Gabrielle, is nothing interesting, the conflicts are not well justified and the hero's nine hundred years of past are just boring. <br /><br />The second book gets a little better. The heroine is more charming with a better constructed past, an amazing breedmate ability but still a little annoying. Dante, the hero, is less conflicted, more practical and just provides a better story than the first. <br /><br />In the end of the second installment, it's clear to anyone that the bland Elise would be paired with the strong and mysterious Tegan. <br /><br />After two books that featured a great idea poorly explored and the promise of a dull heroine you think to give up, I know I did, but hold on just a little. The third book is a surprise for those with patience to get to it. <br /><br />I thought that Elise would never serve for a good heroine in the delicate way she's presented first, blushing for a stronger draft of air and shocked by any foul language. Boy, was I wrong? <br /><br />Elise is so far the best heroine in the series: courageous, practical and mature. She's not a super woman, she has her flaws, some insecurities but nothing overplayed and all perfectly normal to a woman in her position. She's also one of the few heroines I've ever read who's stubborn without being stupid - this is an amazing achievement for the author, most don't get the difference. <br /><br />Tegan is just as interesting as he's supposed to be: an idol to anyone watching his warrior skills, haunted by his past and seething with the idea of getting involved with a female. <br /><br />This plot line is the best one as well, efficiently built and engaging. Adrian manages to explain some things left from the past stories, adding important details to the series as a whole and finally creates a captivating mystery. It's also the first one you don't get excessive pages of doubts and the main characters thinking of insignificant problems that won't get them anywhere. In this one they are either facing something important for the Order or doing something about their relationship, even if it's fighting. Great betterment. <br /><br />I believe Adrian is getting more into the story as she goes, considering more details and how they'll develop further in the plot. There are still details thrown in the mix that end up insignificant in the end or just forgotten, like the relationship between Elise and Chase. It was an important part of the second book, it shows up on this one but nothing really happens, not even a conversation meaningful enough to be thought as closure. I thought the battle in the end was a bit of an anti-climax, surely after everything that drove to that moment it could have been at least more detailed. I still maintain my opinion that Adrian could use a bit more of description on her scenes, most places they go are just left to the reader to invent how they want it to be. It's an option some authors choose but when creating a whole fantastic society, you should expect a bit more of a guideline. As I said before about the other books, I'm still trying to figure out how a Darkhaven looks like. <br /><br />Apart from that I was pleasantly surprised with this book, either if it was for lack of expectations or for it's betterment I can't really say, but I suspect this series is heading to be a good one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13780712484784841904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_4701550'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4701550-passion-unleashed"><img alt="Passion Unleashed (Demonica #3)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1344267582l/4701550._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sJ/2OT2ce1SkbJwFoQbYklqLBdHdXKvXQDnxXWph/BGKuZ/rhsKyPANHKGRW89JNjNTiGRPRJbAbR7fspyIOiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YQahL/ucAyfxGw47NCdQ53v4pLFp6+VGIb4b+IoWsf1bIMj9QMLKT1YwulrD0lo4radDeadmayF6wF1JR1VDZw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13739791964790047842"><b>LARA ADRIAN</b> is a <i>New York Times</i> and #1 internationally best-selling author with nearly 4 million books in print and digital worldwide and translations licensed to more than 20 countries. Her books have been named among Amazon’s Top Ten Romances of the Year, and have also been nominated by readers multiple times as finalists for the Goodreads Choice Award for Best Romance of the Year. Reviewers hav</span>
  <span id="freeText13739791964790047842" style="display:none"><b>LARA ADRIAN</b> is a <i>New York Times</i> and #1 internationally best-selling author with nearly 4 million books in print and digital worldwide and translations licensed to more than 20 countries. Her books have been named among Amazon’s Top Ten Romances of the Year, and have also been nominated by readers multiple times as finalists for the Goodreads Choice Award for Best Romance of the Year. Reviewers have called Lara’s books “addictively readable” (Chicago Tribune), “extraordinary” (Fresh Fiction), “strikingly original” (Booklist), and “one of the best vampire series on the market” (Romantic Times).<br /> <br />Writing as <b>TINA ST. JOHN</b>, her historical romances have won numerous awards including the National Readers Choice; Romantic Times Magazine Reviewer’s Choice; Booksellers Best; and many others. She was twice named a Finalist in Romance Writers of America’s RITA Awards, for Best Historical Romance (White Lion’s Lady) and Best Paranormal Romance (Heart of the Hunter). More recently, the German translation of Heart of the Hunter debuted on Der Spiegel bestseller list.<br /><br />With an ancestry stretching back to the Mayflower and the court of King Henry VIII, the author lives with her husband in New England, where she is working on her next novel. Visit Lara’s website and sign up for new release announcements at <a href="http://bit.ly/LaraAdrianNews" rel="nofollow noopener">http://bit.ly/LaraAdrianNews</a><br /></span>
